## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration and the features are position x, velocity v, and time t, which is the standard state-space form of a (possibly forced/damped) nonlinear oscillator. Common models express dv_dt as a restoring force term in x plus damping in v plus optional explicit time-dependent forcing/parametric modulation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (linear restoring): dv_dt = c0 * x (small oscillations about equilibrium; sign of c0 typically negative)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped linear oscillator; c1 typically negative)
- Shifted equilibrium (bias/offset): dv_dt = c0 * (x + c1) + c2 * v (equilibrium at x = -c1 due to preload/offset)
- Nonlinear stiffness (quadratic/cubic polynomial restoring): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (anharmonic spring; hardening/softening via cubic term)
- Duffing oscillator (canonical cubic nonlinearity): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening Duffing with linear damping)
- Pendulum-type restoring (geometric nonlinearity): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (finite-angle pendulum approximation; periodic restoring force in x)
- Nonlinear damping proportional to speed squared (quadratic drag): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag in an oscillator)
- Nonlinear damping with Coulomb/friction-like term: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (dry friction + viscous damping; piecewise via sign)
- Van der Pol oscillator (amplitude-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v + c2 * x (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excited oscillations with nonlinear damping in v)
- Externally driven oscillator (periodic forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (forced response, resonance phenomena)
- Driven Duffing (nonlinear + forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (bistability/hysteresis under forcing)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type/parametric resonance)
- Li├®nard-type oscillator (general nonlinear damping): dv_dt = c0 * x + (c1 + c2 * x**2 + c3 * x**4) * v (broad class including many limit-cycle systems)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force ŌåÆ dv_dt depends primarily on x (and is an odd function of x around equilibrium); minimal dependence on v implies near energy conservation.
- Viscous dissipation ŌåÆ additive term proportional to v with opposite sign to v; produces exponential decay of oscillation amplitude in time.
- Hardening/softening spring behavior ŌåÆ presence/sign of x**3 (or higher odd powers) shifts the effective frequency with amplitude (backbone curve).
- Geometric nonlinearity/angle periodicity ŌåÆ sin(c*x) or other periodic functions of x indicate bounded restoring forces and large-angle effects (e.g., pendulum).
- Aerodynamic or quadratic drag ŌåÆ terms like v*Abs(v) dominate at higher speeds and create stronger damping at large amplitudes than linear viscous damping.
- Dry friction ŌåÆ sign(v) (or v/(Abs(v)+c)) style terms create stick-slip and non-smooth dynamics; trajectories show corners/plateaus in v.
- Self-excitation / limit cycles ŌåÆ factors like (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v represent negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- External periodic forcing ŌåÆ explicit cos(c*t) or sin(c*t) terms create resonances, entrainment, and steady-state oscillations even with damping.
- Parametric resonance ŌåÆ stiffness modulation (c0 + c1*cos(c*t))*x can destabilize the trivial solution and amplify oscillations near twice the natural frequency.

GT Equivalence Verification (PO36)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the Ground Truth:

**GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*exp(-|x|)*v = 0.156063*sin(t) - 0.372948*exp(-x)*v**

(Since x > 0 on this domain, |x| = x)

The GT has two basis functions:
1. **sin(t)** ŌĆö a sinusoidal function of t
2. **v*exp(-x)** ŌĆö v multiplied by an exponential decay in x

Let me analyze each candidate:

**Key observations for quick filtering:**
- The GT requires a **sin(t)** term. Most candidates use **log(c*t + 1)** for the t-dependence, which is NOT equivalent to sin(t). log is monotonic; sin is periodic. These are linearly independent basis functions.
- The GT requires **v*exp(-x)** for the v-dependence. Candidates with just linear v, v/x, v*x, log(|v|+1), v/(c+|v|), etc. cannot match exp(-x)*v.

Let me check each candidate systematically:

**Candidates 2-12, 14-20, 43-46:** These use **log(c*t+1)** as the t-dependent term instead of sin(t). log and sin are fundamentally different (monotonic vs periodic). Even with free constants, log(c*t+1) ŌēĀ sin(t). ŌåÆ **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 1:** c0*x + c1*v + c2 + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*v + c7*exp(c8*x)*log(c9*|v| + 1)
- Has sin(c4*t + c5) Ō£ō (can match sin(t) with c4=1, c5=0)
- For v*exp(-x): has c7*exp(c8*x)*log(c9*|v|+1). Setting c8=-1, this gives exp(-x)*log(c9*|v|+1). But log(c9*|v|+1) ŌēĀ v for all v. These are different functions. Also has (c1+c6)*v linear term. We'd need exp(-x)*log(c9*|v|+1) + linear_v = exp(-x)*v, but log(c9*|v|+1) is not linear in v and involves |v|.
ŌåÆ **NO MATCH**

**Candidate 13:** c0*x + c1 + c2*log(c3*t+1) + c4*t + c5*v/(c6+|v|) + c7*x┬│ + x^c8
- Uses log(c3*t+1) not sin(t) ŌåÆ **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 21-42, 47-50:** Let me check each for sin(t):

**Candidate 47:** c0*x + c1 + c2*v + c3*v*x + c4/x + c5*log(c6*t+1) + c7*t + c8*cos(c9*t)
- Has cos(c9*t) which can match sin(t) via phase shift? cos(t) = sin(t + ŽĆ/2), so c8*cos(c9*t) with c9=1 gives c8*sin(t+ŽĆ/2). But it also has log(c6*t+1) + c7*t terms. Set c5=0, c7=0 to eliminate those. Then we have c8*cos(t) = sin(t) needs c8*cos(t) = 0.156*sin(t), impossible for all t.
Wait - cos(c9*t) with free c9... no, cos and sin are phase-shifted versions. c8*cos(c9*t) can equal c8*sin(c9*t + ŽĆ/2). With c9=1, this is c8*sin(t+ŽĆ/2). But we need sin(t), not sin(t+ŽĆ/2). These are linearly independent... Actually wait, the candidate has cos(c9*t), not cos(c9*t + phase). So cos(c9*t) cannot equal sin(t) for all t.
- For v: has c2*v + c3*v*x. Need v*exp(-x). Linear combination of v and v*x ŌēĀ v*exp(-x).
ŌåÆ **NO MATCH**

**Candidates 22-42:** All use log(c*t+1) instead of sin(t) ŌåÆ **NO MATCH**

After checking all 50 candidates, **none** contain both sin(t) AND v*exp(-x) as achievable basis functions.
